## Analysis

The GT expression, after substituting constants, is:

```
0.4771*P*sin(0.7761*t) + 0.4455*(1 - P/51.06)*P + 0.4455*P
```

Expanding:
```
0.4771*P*sin(0.7761*t) + 0.4455*P - 0.008726*P² + 0.4455*P
```

Simplifying:
```
-0.008726*P² + 0.8909*P + 0.4771*P*sin(0.7761*t)
```

This is of the form: `a*P² + b*P + c*P*sin(d*t)` where a, b, c, d are specific constants.

Now let me check candidates for a match:

**Candidate 1**: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5 + c6/t^(1/5) + c7 + c8/(P + c9)`

Setting c6=0, c7=0, c8=0, c4=0, this becomes: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t) + P*c5` = `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c5) + P*c2*sin(c3*t)`. This matches with c0=-0.008726, c1+c5=0.8909, c2=0.4771, c3=0.7761, c4=0. ✓

**Candidate 6**: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7) + c8`

Setting c5=0, c8=0, c4=0: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t)`. This matches with c0=-0.008726, c1=0.8909, c2=0.4771, c3=0.7761. ✓

**Candidate 13**: `P*c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + P*c3 + P^c4*c5`

Setting c2=0: `P*c0*sin(c1*t) + P*c3 + c5*P^c4`. Setting c4=2: `P*c0*sin(c1*t) + P*c3 + c5*P²`. This gives `c5*P² + c3*P + c0*P*sin(c1*t)`, matching with c5=-0.008726, c3=0.8909, c0=0.4771, c1=0.7761. ✓

**Candidate 45**: `P*c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + P^c3*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*t + c8)`

Setting c2=0, c5=0, c6=0: `P*c0*sin(c1*t) + c4*P^c3`. With c3=1 this gives only linear P terms (missing P²). But we need both P and P² terms. We can't get both from `c4*P^c3` with a single c3. However, setting c3=2 gives P² but no linear P term. So this doesn't match unless we use the sin term differently... No match.

Multiple candidates match. The cleanest matches are **Candidates 1, 6, and 13**.

Conclusion: Match found

### Candidate 5: `P²*c0 + P*c1/(P + c2) + P*c3*cos(c4*t + c5) + c6*t/(c7 + t²)`
Set c6=0. P²*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*cos(c4*t+c5). Now P*c1/(P+c2) = c1*P/(P+c2). Finding common denominator: c1*P/(P+c2) = c1*(P+c2-c2)/(P+c2) = c1 - c1*c2/(P+c2). This gives a constant plus a term 1/(P+c2), not a P term. Combined with P²*c0: P²*c0 + c1 - c1*c2/(P+c2). We need a P term. Let me reconsider using common denominator with P²*c0: (P²*c0*(P+c2) + P*c1)/(P+c2) = (c0*P³ + c0*c2*P² + c1*P)/(P+c2). GT would be (P+c2)*(c_a*P² + c_b*P) = c_a*P³ + (c_a*c2+c_b)*P² + c_b*c2*P. So c0=c_a, c1=c_b*c2, c_a*c2+c_b = 0 → c2 = -c_b/c_a ≈ 102.1. c1 = c_b*102.1 ≈ 91.0. But we also need the sin term to factor as P*c3*cos(...)*(P+c2)/(P+c2), which doesn't work since the sin term multiplied by (P+c2) introduces P²*sin. So this doesn't simplify cleanly. Actually, the terms aren't over a common denominator - they're added separately. So: P²*c0 + c1 - c1*c2/(P+c2) + P*c3*cos(...). Missing the linear P term (can't get it from remaining terms).
**Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]**
